Having drunk the elixir of life, he is now Ramses the Damned, doomed forever to wander the earth, desperate to quell hungers that can never be satisfied. Although he pursues voluptuous aristocrat Julie Stratford, the woman for whom he desperately longs is Cleopatra. And his intense longing for her, undiminished over the centuries, will force him to commit an act that will place everyone around him in the gravest danger....</span>

Popular Answered Questions

<div class="communityQuestion">
<div class="questionText">
<a href="/questions/411522-why-does-the-book-end-with-to-be">Why does the book end with "to be continued" when it was never continued!!???</a>
</div>
<div class="communityQAFooter questionFooter">
<ul class="questionFooterActions">
<li class="footerItem like">
<span id="like_container_community_question_411522" class="likeItContainer"><a href="http://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F159501.The_Mummy" class="jsLike like_it" rel="nofollow">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class="footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp">
<a href="/questions/411522-why-does-the-book-end-with-to-be">8 months ago</a>
</li>
<li class="footerItem communityQuestionPermalink">
<a href="/questions/411522-why-does-the-book-end-with-to-be">Add your answer</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class="allCommunityAnswers">
<div class="communityAnswer">
<div class="communityAnswerBody">
<div class="answererUserIcon">
<a href="/user/show/31599570-james-zieff" class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto"><img src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/users/1400724552i/31599570._UY100_CR9,0,100,100_.jpg" alt="" /></a>
</div>
<div class="communityAnswerTextContainer">
<span class="communityAnswererName">
<a href="/user/show/31599570-james-zieff">James Zieff</a>
</span>
<span class="communityAnswerText">
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">the original story was supposed to be a movie but was withdrawn and turned into the book. the intention was to publish at least one sequel but it<a href="#" class="jsShow showAction">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">the original story was supposed to be a movie but was withdrawn and turned into the book. the intention was to publish at least one sequel but it never happened because the book didn't sell real well. there is a note on Anne Rice's webpage that she recently turned back to this universe and may finally write that long-awaited sequel.<a href="#" class="jsHide hideAction">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_482570937">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/482570937" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5518809-madeline-knight-dixon" class="left imgcol" title="Madeline Knight-Dixon"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1308587835p2/5518809.jpg" alt="Madeline Knight-Dixon" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/482570937?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 21, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5518809-madeline-knight-dixon" class="user" title="Madeline Knight-Dixon">Madeline Knight-Dixon</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/43782.The_Mummy" title=" 9780099471370" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer482570937">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer287495672545607944">I give you the book the movie The Mummy was SUPPOSED to be based off of. In the end they butchered the story so much Anne Rice wouldn’t put her name on it. Which is a shame, because this book is (if not better) sexier than the movie.<br /><br />A lot of reviews call it “vintage Anne Rice” and I couldn’t agree more. It gets back to the feel of Interview with the Vampire; darkly sexual with the most compelling plot. She’s seriously one of the best storytellers of all time.<br /><br />A mummy rises, he falls in love, and</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText287495672545607944">I give you the book the movie The Mummy was SUPPOSED to be based off of. In the end they butchered the story so much Anne Rice wouldn’t put her name on it. Which is a shame, because this book is (if not better) sexier than the movie.<br /><br />A lot of reviews call it “vintage Anne Rice” and I couldn’t agree more. It gets back to the feel of Interview with the Vampire; darkly sexual with the most compelling plot. She’s seriously one of the best storytellers of all time.<br /><br />A mummy rises, he falls in love, and they journey to Egypt where he misuses his immortal elixer. Seems like it would be cheesy or at least silly. But nothing about this is like that-everything about this book makes sense. The way he rises, the way he acts, how long he’s lived, he’s relationship with Cleopatra, how he learns to operate the modern world. Every aspect of the story has a logical explanation laid out clearly within the story. (In my opinion there’s nothing worse than an author having to explain themselves after the book is published *coughStephenieMeyercough*)<br /><br />Just like all of Rice’s other works, Ramses is devastatingly perfect. The woman he falls in love with is fierce and intelligent without being cliche. There’s an older man that for some reason you are attracted to, despite his age. An adorable innocent young man for you to obsess over, and the quintessential bad boy that you can’t help but love. Add in a dangerous and alluring female villain and you’ve got one of the sexiest cast of characters I’ve ever read.<br /><br />The book is fairly long, but Rice is always a fast read. I’ve always found Anne Rice to be the perfect alternative to a “fluff” book because even though there’s elements of a romance novel, the plot is still the most important part of the story. It’s fast-paced and oh so fun.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="287495672545607944">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

This novel is no exception, as it was written at the height of her talents. There's something glamorous about this book and how it was written.       <a href="/user/show/298306-katie" class="user" title="Katie">Katie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/43782.The_Mummy" title=" 9780099471370" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/298306-katie?shelf=awesomeauthors" class="actionLinkLite">awesomeauthors</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/298306-katie?shelf=historical" class="actionLinkLite">historical</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/298306-katie?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer8400014">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15815798249573466049">Can't believe it took me so long to read this one. There are only one or two of Rice's books that I haven't liked, but this one was classic Rice. She captures the historical mood perfectly, the grandeur and romance and mystery, the eroticism that is somehow woven into every scene, without being trite or distracting. Just when I think I know how she's going to resolve things, she goes in a completely different -- yet perfectly fitting and satisfying -- direction. There are a lot of themes in this</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15815798249573466049">Can't believe it took me so long to read this one. There are only one or two of Rice's books that I haven't liked, but this one was classic Rice. She captures the historical mood perfectly, the grandeur and romance and mystery, the eroticism that is somehow woven into every scene, without being trite or distracting. Just when I think I know how she's going to resolve things, she goes in a completely different -- yet perfectly fitting and satisfying -- direction. There are a lot of themes in this one that echo the vampires, which was neat to see. I'm not sure which came first, though I suspect vampires were her first love. <br /><br />This novel is the story of Ramses, an immortal mummy who is brought back to life unknowingly by the archeologist who discovers his tomb. It then follows him and the humans who know his secret from England to Egypt, and ponders what will become of the remaining immortality elixir. I recommend this one to anyone who loves Rice, or historical fantasy that isn't too "fantasy". </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15815798249573466049">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_172670980">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/172670980" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3555710-marianne" class="left imgcol" title="Marianne"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1306897412p2/3555710.jpg" alt="Marianne" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/172670980?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 31, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3555710-marianne" class="user" title="Marianne">Marianne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/57860.The_Mummy_Or_Rameses_The_Damned" title="Hardcover 9780701135386" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3555710-marianne?shelf=fantasy-horror-sci-fi" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy-horror-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer172670980">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4998469594299699943">Before I rant, a little background: I’ve always enjoyed horror stories, in particular, vampire and mummy stories. As a young teen my favorite author was H.P. Lovecraft, and one of my most favorite horror stories was <em>The Jewel of Seven Stars</em> by Bram Stoker which is a “mummy” story. Starting in 1984 I began reading what came to be known as “The Vampire Chronicles” by Anne Rice. The first book, <em>Interview With the Vampire</em>, was sensuous and atmospheric and rewrote traditional vampire mythology. Intri</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4998469594299699943">Before I rant, a little background: I’ve always enjoyed horror stories, in particular, vampire and mummy stories. As a young teen my favorite author was H.P. Lovecraft, and one of my most favorite horror stories was <em>The Jewel of Seven Stars</em> by Bram Stoker which is a “mummy” story. Starting in 1984 I began reading what came to be known as “The Vampire Chronicles” by Anne Rice. The first book, <em>Interview With the Vampire</em>, was sensuous and atmospheric and rewrote traditional vampire mythology. Intrigued, I immediately moved to the second book, <em>The Vampire Lestat</em>, which was a natural continuation of the mythology, and then snapped up the third book, <em>Queen of the Damned</em>, as soon as it hit bookstore shelves in 1988. And that brings us to my thoughts about <em>The Mummy</em>. I read <em>The Mummy</em> while waiting for the next installment of the vampire books hoping to find Rice giving mummies the same unique treatment that she’d given to vampires. Nope. <em>The Mummy</em> read more like an outline of a book -- something she probably pitched to her editor and had published quickly to capitalize on the vampire books. The premise was compelling but the writing is purely awful. Sentence fragments and other bad grammar, cheesy melodramatic scenes, trite dialog, and a tendency to slip into the style of cheap pornography insulted not only my intelligence but my sensibilities throughout. Yeah, I read the whole thing hoping it would get better as the story unfolded. It didn’t.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4998469594299699943">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer130921234">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1341009806749160013">OK, I'm giving it one star but I did read it all the way through.<br /><br />I thought this headed towards pulp, not up to the quality of her other books (and a bit more towards porn-lit).<br /><br />Also, I guess I can be nit picky, but Ramses claims that his cells can't die. He gives an example of using the elixir on plants hoping that his subjects will be able to eat forever, but the awful thing is that the plants regrow in people's stomachs. Awful picture, but I state it just to point out that she's trying to make</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1341009806749160013">OK, I'm giving it one star but I did read it all the way through.<br /><br />I thought this headed towards pulp, not up to the quality of her other books (and a bit more towards porn-lit).<br /><br />Also, I guess I can be nit picky, but Ramses claims that his cells can't die. He gives an example of using the elixir on plants hoping that his subjects will be able to eat forever, but the awful thing is that the plants regrow in people's stomachs. Awful picture, but I state it just to point out that she's trying to make a point.<br /><br />It seems to me, however, that Anne misses this point when Ramses and the female lead have sex. I kept waiting for he woman to get pregnant. I mean, his sperm would never die right, so there'd be a billion of them waiting in those fallopian tubes for the next egg to come by. I pictured her getting pregnant with his children for the rest of her child bearing years.<br /><br />OK, I guess I took it too literally. My bad.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15959831862300319017">I was stuck in a library waiting and had nothing to read. I picked this up thinking 'Ancient Egypt, the undead, how can it be bad?' without looking at the author.<br /><br />After first few pages I checked. Oh dear.<br /><br />I really do not like Anne Rice.<br /><br />It was in reading this book for a few hours stuck in a library and continuing out of an awful sense of self harm that I realised that Anne Rice wants to be immortal. She doesn't care how she manages to do it, she wants to be undead. Not in the horror awful monster way either, as she romanticizes the awesome classic villain archetype. But in a beautiful way. And I'm pretty sure she wants to be a gay man.<br /></span>

          <a href="/book/show/43782.The_Mummy" title=" 9780099471370" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer348573802">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11465717393825217493">First, I'm a middle-aged guy who does not read bodice-rippers as a rule. Perhaps "ever" is a better word. But I happen to love mummy fiction, be it in the form of a movie or a book. That was what prompted me to dive into Anne Rice's "The Mummy," which, prior to "The Da Vinci Code," was the worst book I could not put down. Perhaps anticipating the Brendan Fraser Mummy movies that came along several years later, this Mummy is not a shriveled, bandaged, mute zombie hit man, stumping around and stra</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11465717393825217493">First, I'm a middle-aged guy who does not read bodice-rippers as a rule. Perhaps "ever" is a better word. But I happen to love mummy fiction, be it in the form of a movie or a book. That was what prompted me to dive into Anne Rice's "The Mummy," which, prior to "The Da Vinci Code," was the worst book I could not put down. Perhaps anticipating the Brendan Fraser Mummy movies that came along several years later, this Mummy is not a shriveled, bandaged, mute zombie hit man, stumping around and strangling anyone that has p.o.'d some guy in a Fez; he's a reconstituted, perfectly modern-looking, very verbose heartthrob who happens to be secretly a few thousand years old. And therein lies the rub, at least for me: what follows is a post-Edwardian romance novel with some of the most excruciating dialogue on record; Leslie Nielsen should have done the audio book. And yet, I kept turning the pages, in spite of myself. So if you, like me, prefer the likes of a prunefaced beswathed nightmare, dragging his foot behind him as he shambles his way to his next victim, then you may be disappointed in this reincarnation, even though the adventure aspect of the story holds interest. If, however, you're sick of dashing Byronic vampires and want to try a dashing Byronic mummy, who melts the heart of a panting, virginal heroine with a penchant for spouting lines that even Judi Dench couldn't sell, then this is the book for you. "Reader, I buried him!"</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11465717393825217493">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8280657770383296678">Leido... Y la verdad es que me esperaba más y solamente le doy un aprobado...<br /><br />La novela aunque empieza de forma prometedora enseguida la historia se estanca y se vuelva lenta y monótoma. No es hasta pasada la página 300 (mi edición de bolsillo tiene 541 págs.) que la cosa se anima un poco, pues la acción y la tensión van in crescendo conforme llega el final. El desenlace no está mal: es abierto y lógico aunque para mi gusto, poco singular...<br /><br />El estilo de Anne Rice hace la lectura amena y rápida. A</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8280657770383296678">Leido... Y la verdad es que me esperaba más y solamente le doy un aprobado...<br /><br />La novela aunque empieza de forma prometedora enseguida la historia se estanca y se vuelva lenta y monótoma. No es hasta pasada la página 300 (mi edición de bolsillo tiene 541 págs.) que la cosa se anima un poco, pues la acción y la tensión van in crescendo conforme llega el final. El desenlace no está mal: es abierto y lógico aunque para mi gusto, poco singular...<br /><br />El estilo de Anne Rice hace la lectura amena y rápida. Aunque la historia en algunas fase sea monótona se deja leer bien. Sabiendo que las comparaciones son odiosa en ciertos momentos me hizo pensar en Robin Cook...<br /><br />Siendo como soy amante del género de terror esta novela la he encontrado un poco ñoña para mi gusto, explota poco el potencial terrorífico que una momia podría tener.<br /><br />Con todo, resumiendo, como lectura amena, sin buscar muchas pretenciones literarias y si te atrae vivir una historia ambientada en el Egipto de la época victoriana, este es tu libro. Un libro normalito que entiendo que no sea de lo más conocido de Anne Rice...<br />Le pongo un 3 sobre 5.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4347969719939669153">The Mummy: Ramses the Damned - VG<br />Anne Rice - Standalone<br /><br />Ramses the Great has awakened in Edwardian London. Having drunk the elixir of life, he is now Ramses the Damned, doomed forever to wander the earth, desperate to quell hungers that can never be satisfied. <span id="freeTextContainer10594857547688587932">This is the second time I have read this book, as the last time was years ago. The story is different then any mummy tale I have seen to date. It deals more so with immortality then raising the dead, and the emotional turmoil that accompanies being immortal. <br /><br />The Story moves quickly and the characters are very likeable. The reason I only gave the book four stars is because three quarters of the way through the book, I found the characters where not behaving quite like themselves and also because</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10594857547688587932">This is the second time I have read this book, as the last time was years ago. The story is different then any mummy tale I have seen to date. It deals more so with immortality then raising the dead, and the emotional turmoil that accompanies being immortal. <br /><br />The Story moves quickly and the characters are very likeable. The reason I only gave the book four stars is because three quarters of the way through the book, I found the characters where not behaving quite like themselves and also because I find I'm left hanging at the end of the book. I feel robbed of the knowledge of what happens to certain characters like Alex? Elliot? <br /><br />I feel the book has been left open for a sequel but so far there has been non forthcoming. With Anne Rice I guess you just can't ever tell what she will do next. Crossing my fingers, but not holding my breath.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_31642269">

  <a href="/user/show/1359426-mojca" class="left imgcol" title="Mojca"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1379576265p2/1359426.jpg" alt="Mojca" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/31642269?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 13, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1359426-mojca" class="user" title="Mojca">Mojca</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1359426-mojca?shelf=paranormal-romance-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">paranormal-romance-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1359426-mojca?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1359426-mojca?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer31642269">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer988223869422026153">I don't particularly like Ms. Rice's vampire storylines, so I was pleasantly surprised by the theme in this book, so completely removed from the vampiric realm, yet still firmly entrenched in the paranormal genre.<br /><br />I'm a big fan of mummies (from cartoons, movies, to books) and Ramses the Damned with his soulful blue eyes is no exception. I loved his story, the trials and tribulations he had to go through and I was rooting for him from the beginning...And was so very happy he got his just reward.<br /><br />A</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText988223869422026153">I don't particularly like Ms. Rice's vampire storylines, so I was pleasantly surprised by the theme in this book, so completely removed from the vampiric realm, yet still firmly entrenched in the paranormal genre.<br /><br />I'm a big fan of mummies (from cartoons, movies, to books) and Ramses the Damned with his soulful blue eyes is no exception. I loved his story, the trials and tribulations he had to go through and I was rooting for him from the beginning...And was so very happy he got his just reward.<br /><br />A wonderful, gripping, intense, rather poetic, romantic, angsty, dramatic novel.</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer84103154">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer212501255753065730">I really like how "The Mummy" started out, and I had high hopes for it. Anne Rice is so good with suspense. The characters seemed full and precise, and I thought the plot was intriguing. However, as soon as the characters disembarked (and you'll know what I'm talking about if you read the book), the story falls on its face. The characters don't follow their established personalities, and the story turns into a circus on a merry-go-round. I've read worse, but I really expected better of this book</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText212501255753065730">I really like how "The Mummy" started out, and I had high hopes for it. Anne Rice is so good with suspense. The characters seemed full and precise, and I thought the plot was intriguing. However, as soon as the characters disembarked (and you'll know what I'm talking about if you read the book), the story falls on its face. The characters don't follow their established personalities, and the story turns into a circus on a merry-go-round. I've read worse, but I really expected better of this book.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_140663737">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140663737" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3616303-j-c" class="left imgcol" title="J.C."><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442517981p2/3616303.jpg" alt="J.C." /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/140663737?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 13, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3616303-j-c" class="user" title="J.C.">J.C.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/43782.The_Mummy" title=" 9780099471370" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer140663737">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15511602661135764963">This was a book highly recommended. It’s also the first Anne Rice I’ve ever read.<br /><br />After finishing this novel, I’m don’t feel it’s representative of her best work.<br /><br />Not that it’s that bad. The beginning popped for me and I was thoroughly engrossed in the story and characters. Bascially, this is a love story between a mummy brought to live and the daughter of the man who freed him from his tomb.<br /><br />Sounds…unique. And it is. But to a point.<br /><br />By the time Ramses and his modern love Julie return to Egypt, I wa</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15511602661135764963">This was a book highly recommended. It’s also the first Anne Rice I’ve ever read.<br /><br />After finishing this novel, I’m don’t feel it’s representative of her best work.<br /><br />Not that it’s that bad. The beginning popped for me and I was thoroughly engrossed in the story and characters. Bascially, this is a love story between a mummy brought to live and the daughter of the man who freed him from his tomb.<br /><br />Sounds…unique. And it is. But to a point.<br /><br />By the time Ramses and his modern love Julie return to Egypt, I was a little peeved at the way some of the characters and their storyline were being handled. Not to mention feeling that some of the subplots were more distracting than they should have been.<br /><br />I had to remind myself I’m not reading a piece of literature that requires such scrutiny. In letting go of these prejudices, I did enjoy the read more, but not enough to post a rave review about it.<br /><br />The last part of the book, just couldn’t keep me page turning like I did in the beginning.<br /><br />I can see why she’s a popular writer and I look forward to reading the Mayfair witch series. I also cannot wait to finally read Interview With A Vampire.<br /><br />So this wasn’t a bad introduction and I’m crossing my fingers I learn to like Anne Rice as much as her fans. I see the potential, but time will tell.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15511602661135764963">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17073040160705582371">I'd found <a title="Servant of the Bones by Anne Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43805.Servant_of_the_Bones">Servant of the Bones</a> in my university library and had enjoyed it greatly, so I thought I'd let <a title="Anne Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice">Anne Rice</a> entertain me again with a book about one of my greatest interests, Egypt. She didn't.<br /><br />Because of the settings and locations--early 1900s London and Egypt--and the characters--a murdered British archeologist and the main character, his Edwardian daughter--I kept thinking (or hoping) I was reading an <a title="Elizabeth Peters" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16549.Elizabeth_Peters">Elizabeth Peters</a> novel. But I every time I thought it, I was reminded that it sadly wa</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17073040160705582371">I'd found <a title="Servant of the Bones by Anne Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43805.Servant_of_the_Bones">Servant of the Bones</a> in my university library and had enjoyed it greatly, so I thought I'd let <a title="Anne Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice">Anne Rice</a> entertain me again with a book about one of my greatest interests, Egypt. She didn't.<br /><br />Because of the settings and locations--early 1900s London and Egypt--and the characters--a murdered British archeologist and the main character, his Edwardian daughter--I kept thinking (or hoping) I was reading an <a title="Elizabeth Peters" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16549.Elizabeth_Peters">Elizabeth Peters</a> novel. But I every time I thought it, I was reminded that it sadly wasn't by the utter <em>badness</em> that was everywhere in this book. There was the badness of the writing, the characterization, the story, and probably other things that I can't even remember anymore. It was basically a romance novel.</span>

  <a href="/user/show/5500406-brianna" class="left imgcol" title="brianna"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1405910013p2/5500406.jpg" alt="brianna" /></a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1021872899">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11455399692881322477">In many ways The Mummy is atypical of Anne Rice, and yet totally typical. I love that it taps into a genre of film especially that is culturally familiar and tells this engaging story about immorality and history.<br /><br />That being said, I read this for the first time when I was pretty young, and I don't recall disliking Ramses or Julie as much as I did this time around. I understand that Julie is a woman of her times - and supposedly ahead of her times - but she just irritates me. Her mewling suitor Al</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11455399692881322477">In many ways The Mummy is atypical of Anne Rice, and yet totally typical. I love that it taps into a genre of film especially that is culturally familiar and tells this engaging story about immorality and history.<br /><br />That being said, I read this for the first time when I was pretty young, and I don't recall disliking Ramses or Julie as much as I did this time around. I understand that Julie is a woman of her times - and supposedly ahead of her times - but she just irritates me. Her mewling suitor Alex isn't much better, and Ramses is entirely a hedonistic narcissist, which makes he and Julie's sudden monogamy strange. <br /><br />It's also a bit irritating that Rice glosses over the colonialism and cultural invasion that is pretty inherent in the 'exploration' of Egypt, and 'discovery' of Pharaoh's tombs during this time. She seems to just decide that's a blind spot she can live with, and not even nod to, even though it would've given the novel a lot more depth and added interest - especially with Ramses awakening into an entirely new world - his feelings about Egypt's changes are pretty superficial, and since he's supposed to be this highly intelligent, philosophical immortal man, it seems strange he'd just basically have an emo spell after seeing "modern" Egypt (which is pretty much fixed by sex, of course).<br /><br />Basically everyone in this novel is annoying as hell, with maybe the exception of Elliott, especially given his romantic partners of the past, and his bizarre half-dead/rotting sex scene with the newly risen Cleopatra.<br /><br />This is a book that is great for Anne Rice fans. I'm lukewarm on Anne Rice but I really do love her contribution and even foundation-laying of the paranormal/vampire genre.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11455399692881322477">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_938100988">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/938100988" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/27987005-tinka" class="left imgcol" title="Tinka"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1390519559p2/27987005.jpg" alt="Tinka" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/938100988?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 19, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/27987005-tinka" class="user" title="Tinka">Tinka</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/43782.The_Mummy" title=" 9780099471370" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/27987005-tinka?shelf=reviewed-books-new" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed-books-new</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/27987005-tinka?shelf=read-in-german" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-german</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/27987005-tinka?shelf=stand-alone" class="actionLinkLite">stand-alone</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/27987005-tinka?shelf=paperback-hardcover" class="actionLinkLite">paperback-hardcover</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/27987005-tinka?shelf=2-stars-kinda-meh" class="actionLinkLite">2-stars-kinda-meh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer938100988">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14907046998165789666"><strong> <em>“When we are weary, we speak lovingly of dreams as if they embodied our true desires”</em> </strong><br /><br /><strong>Spoilers...duh</strong><br /><br />Right now, I’m letting out a loud groan. That is all I really can do thinking about this book. Well, I could give you a very impressive eye roll as well. Or I pull out some of my hair. <br /><br />This was actually my first Anne Rice book ever. I always wanted to start with the Vampire Chronicles, because I really like the movie adaptation from Interview with the Vampire (it is one of the few movies I actual</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14907046998165789666"><strong>
  <em>“When we are weary, we speak lovingly of dreams as if they embodied our true desires”</em>
</strong><br /><br /><strong>Spoilers...duh</strong><br /><br />Right now, I’m letting out a loud groan. That is all I really can do thinking about this book. Well, I could give you a very impressive eye roll as well. Or I pull out some of my hair. <br /><br />This was actually my first Anne Rice book ever. I always wanted to start with the Vampire Chronicles, because I really like the movie adaptation from Interview with the Vampire (it is one of the few movies I actually don’t mind Tom Cruise) and because a good friend of mine really enjoys the series. But blame it on the Book Gods up there or something, I started with this one…and it made me question if I actually wanna give her other books a go or not.<br /><br />I got this one for free and even if the ending tricks you into believing it is actually part of a series, it is a standalone book and I actually believed it maybe would be better to start with something that is not part of a giant series. Sometimes my ideas are bad. Also, free books are bad as well (sometimes…).<br /><br /><strong>Writing.</strong> It is not that I dislike the writing. It is more that sometimes I found it unintentionally funny. This book basically read like a bad, bad daily soap or at least how I would imagine a novelized version of a script from a bad, bad daily soap. Very short sentences that didn’t feel like they belong anywhere, jumps between action and different POV’s so clumsily done that you actually can only raise an eyebrow and dialogues so flat, cheesy and unrealistic that suddenly even the dialogues from The Spice Girls movie makes more sense. <br /><br />I read somewhere that this was originally planned as a movie script, which probably would’ve made more sense. It would at least explain the weird “cuts” between scenes and parts of the dialogue. Also this book is divided into two parts and a lot of it felt just made up as the story goes along, anything but planned really. So, again if that was originally shorter, intended for the big screen and not as a 400 page novel, it would make more sense. Not that I believe it would have been a good movie, it would have been some B or make that C romantic horror trash, but probably more amusing. Still, I prefer watching the movie with Brendan Fraser and the always lovely Rachel Weisz. <br /><br /><strong>Story.</strong> Like I said before, this book is divided into two parts and therefore mostly into two plots…and a lot of weird subplots.<br /><br />It actually starts very interesting. Hobby archeologist finds tomb of Pharaoh Ramses the 2nd or Ramses the damned, gets murdered by his evil nephew who is after the family’s money, his daughter inherits everything, nephew wants to murder daughter as well, mummy comes to life and saves her. So far, so good. But what actually happens then is basically just summed up with “stuff happens”. <br /><br />There are so many different plots in this book that I got kinda lost. Not because they are too complicated, but because most of them are either dragged out, rushed, not very exciting or seem just to exist to make the book longer. The pacing is way off and so is the sense making. <br /><br />The funny thing to me is that if the second part never happened and the main plot lines were resolved in the first, making the book about 200 hundred pages shorter, it could’ve worked. It still wouldn’t have been a great piece of literature, but at least it would’ve been more than just a messy theme park ride. <br /><br />Sometimes simplicity works much better than complicated (or wannabe complicated) long stories. Why not just focus the story on Ramses adapting to modern London, falling in love with Julie (previously mentioned daughter) and them dealing with Evil Cousin Henry? Why the trip to Egypt, Julie’s lovesick puppy wannabe fiancé, his depressed dad and most of all Zombie Cleopatra (yes, Zombie Cleopatra, I shit you not)? The book would’ve benefited from a tighter, more personal story.<br /><br />Oh, before I forget, let’s talk Genre for a bit. I heard people telling me how wonderful Anne Rice is with writing horror and a living mummy should be the perfect opportunity for that, right? RIGHT? There was no horror in this book. Fine, okay I can live with that. A Mummy story also gives a great opportunity for an adventure. There is no real sense of adventure here. Again fine...how about just using the mysticism of Ancient Egypt? Well…there is some…but not much. This book focuses mostly on romance, which would be fine, if the romance were written well. It is not.<br /><br /><strong>Characters.</strong> Oh boy, those were something else. Like the story, the characters started out pretty interesting but it went downhill the more I got into the book.<br /><br />Our titular Mummy Ramses, or Mr. Ramsay, is a hunk, to make it short. Yes, the creepy old mummy turned out to be a hot guy, intelligent (I think), over the top romantic and with a libido that can compete with bunnies. Oh yeah and he is immortal. What could’ve been a tragic, mysterious, complex anti-hero in a more serious fish out of water story, turned into the romantic lead of some Ancient Egypt soap opera. He was interesting at first, but his behavior, his know it all attitude, the very schmaltzy dialogue and his constant crying over his tortured love life made him simply annoying. He wasn’t “please bury him alive again – annoying” but he didn’t make me want to root for him either.<br /><br />Julie is the one that really frustrated me. She had so much potential and started out great. Described as being at her most beautiful when looking serious, an independent woman that wants to stay on her own two feet and not get married just because society tell her two – bravo! If only she could’ve stayed that way. As soon as she meets Ramses her character changes into a lovesick idiot, whom cannot walk from one room to another without getting help from her super hot man. She constantly needs saving, is needy beyond help, cries her way through the story and is utterly useless all the time. She started out as somewhat of the main character and turns into the nagging girlfriend that cannot live without Ramses anymore. And oh is she stupid. She barely has human reactions to anything. Like for example, she knows her cousin killed her father and does nothing about it. She doesn’t tell her uncle, she doesn’t call the police and she doesn’t let Ramses just kill him, nope she basically waits around for bad karma to get him or fate or whatever. Point is, she changes so drastically throughout the book that she seems like an entirely different character.<br /><br />The other characters are mostly caricatures of people. Henry is evil, treats women badly, drinks, has a gambling problem and well, he is a murder. He is so bad, he makes Tom Buchanan look like sunshine. Then there is Alex, Julie’s sort of boyfriend who desperately wants to marry her. He is like a lost puppy and seems pathetic for most of the book. His father Elliot is probably the most interesting character of them all and somehow even likeable. He is depressed, has problems with his age, is married to a woman even if he is secretly gay and misses his younger years. He is the only character with a certain depth. Then there is Samir. He is the Renfield to Ramses’ Dracula.<br /><br />Of course when talking about characters, I have to talk about Cleopatra. Now comes the part where another deep sigh follows. The might Egyptian Queen becomes a sex obsessed Zombie with more psychological issues than any of the Kardashian’s combined. Instead of playing her story as a deep tragedy, she is just crazy. That’s it. Oh, how the mighty have fallen.<br /><br /><strong>Romance.</strong> Remember when Twilight was published and a lot of people were accusing Stephanie Meyer of stealing from here and there and Anne Rice’s Vampire Chronicles were mentioned quite a few times? Yeah, I guess if she read one book by her, it was more likely this one. <br /><br />Just think about it. Girl meets super hot, mysterious undead guy and falls in love at first sight. He loves her as well but fights his feelings for a while to protect her. Hormones rage. Undying eternal love after knowing each other basically for a few seconds. He struggles with the choice to make her immortal or not. Another powerful creature comes after them. She needs to be saved by him almost 24/7. He is her whole life, everything else doesn’t matter anymore. She is his whole life, everything else doesn’t matter anymore. One of them breaks up with the other, because it is for the best. Girl wants to kill herself rather than being without him, in the end everything turns out peachy.<br /><br />You get what I mean, right? Take that and add a little bit more sex (because as well know in the World of most YA fiction sex is evil) and you have the perfect prototype for Edward and Bella.<br /><br />The romance was terrible and the worst part of this book. Sadly, it was also the largest part. <br /><br />Julie changed completely after meeting Ramses and became just all about him. And Ramses could barely make up his mind who he wanted to be with. Julie? Cleopatra? Well, he banged them both (funnily enough Julie never really said anything about that. Did she know? I can’t remember).<br /><br />In the end Julie briefly breaks up with Ramses because she didn’t want to be immortal and realized their relationship wasn’t good for either of them and too much had happened. I was cheering, I wanted to applaud. It was great and unusual. Of course that single moment of awesomeness had to be destroyed in the next chapter. Julie realizes she can’t live without Ramses and wants to kill herself (which makes complete sense to everything she said before…) but Ramses of course saves her, gives her his magic potion of immortality and the live and screw each other forever and ever and ever.<br /><br />How seriously f****d up is that?<br /><br /><strong>Conclusion:</strong> I hope this is just the black sheep when it comes to Anne Rice’s works. <br /><br /><strong>Recommendation:</strong> Not really, I mean it is worth a few good laughs.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14907046998165789666">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_854829016">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/854829016" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8854256-carrie-slager" class="left imgcol" title="Carrie Slager"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Carrie Slager" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/854829016?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 14, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8854256-carrie-slager" class="user" title="Carrie Slager">Carrie Slager</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/43782.The_Mummy" title=" 9780099471370" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8854256-carrie-slager?shelf=books-i-bought" class="actionLinkLite">books-i-bought</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer854829016">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1111362890474550074">I’ve read a lot of Anne Rice’s books, but The Mummy is my absolute favourite, no question about it. It has the perfect mix of tragedy, romance, history and emotion that Anne Rice pulls off so well, without any extra flab added to the story. Compared to her other novels, The Mummy is incredibly short, with my version only being 398 pages. Believe me, they read fast!<br /><br />Maybe I’m a bit biased because I’ve always loved ancient Egypt and have been fascinated by Ramses the Great. I’m not necessarily an a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1111362890474550074">I’ve read a lot of Anne Rice’s books, but The Mummy is my absolute favourite, no question about it. It has the perfect mix of tragedy, romance, history and emotion that Anne Rice pulls off so well, without any extra flab added to the story. Compared to her other novels, The Mummy is incredibly short, with my version only being 398 pages. Believe me, they read fast!<br /><br />Maybe I’m a bit biased because I’ve always loved ancient Egypt and have been fascinated by Ramses the Great. I’m not necessarily an admirer of him, but he does play a significant role in history and did have an interesting life. Well, Anne Rice brings him to life in The Mummy and he is as charming, well-spoken and lecherous as one would expect. But he also has a soft side, which is what makes it so easy for Julie and readers to fall in love with him. Julie herself has a few too many modern sensibilities for the era, but she is an interesting character because she is so strong. She’s the perfect match for Ramses.<br /><br />Anne Rice showcases exactly what it is that makes people want to devote their entire lives to the study of Egyptology. If you haven’t fallen in love with Egypt by the time you finish The Mummy, you likely never will. I didn’t even catch any glaring historical inaccuracies. Sure, some things were changed around if you believe in the traditional Cleopatra story, but Anne Rice presents a compelling alternative that makes sense in the context of the story. Her vivid descriptions reveal the passion she has for ancient Egypt and that enthusiasm continues throughout the entire novel.<br /><br />Her later Vampire Chronicles works seemed to lack heart, but The Mummy certainly does not. It’s fresh, a fitting retelling of the very old, generally cliché shambling mummy coming back from the grave story. Of course it has fantastical elements, but I don’t think they’ll be overwhelming for people who don’t normally read fantasy. Anne Rice achieved perfect balance in The Mummy and it’s a book I would highly recommend to anyone.<br /><br />Warning: This is an Anne Rice book. Of course there are explicit sex scenes and gore that could be offensive to young or sensitive readers. I would personally not recommend The Mummy for anyone under 14, but everyone matures at different rates. Use your common sense when buying books.<br /><br />I give this book 5/5 stars.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1111362890474550074">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_192295087">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/192295087" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5922167-sheila" class="left imgcol" title="Sheila"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1432506364p2/5922167.jpg" alt="Sheila" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/192295087?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 31, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5922167-sheila" class="user" title="Sheila">Sheila</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5922167-sheila?shelf=rice-anne" class="actionLinkLite">rice-anne</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer192295087">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17934704960175804345">A British archeologist in early 1900's Egypt uncovers a mummy's sarcophagus covered with all manner of dire warnings about disturbing the occupant. Undeterred, the mummy is removed; but instead of the mummy claiming vengeance on anyone, someone else murders the archeologist. The mummy is sent back to England to the home of the archeologist's wealthy daughter for display in her home, and the story takes off from there. <br /><br />I read this book after reading Interview With the Vampire; this is clearly not</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17934704960175804345">A British archeologist in early 1900's Egypt uncovers a mummy's sarcophagus covered with all manner of dire warnings about disturbing the occupant. Undeterred, the mummy is removed; but instead of the mummy claiming vengeance on anyone, someone else murders the archeologist. The mummy is sent back to England to the home of the archeologist's wealthy daughter for display in her home, and the story takes off from there. <br /><br />I read this book after reading Interview With the Vampire; this is clearly not as a high a caliber book as Interview. I liked the author's treatment of the mummy and the issues with immortality. I also liked the creativity of exploring the problems with feeding an elixir of immortality to food sources such as field crops and cattle and the horrifying results. The emotions related to and problems with immortality for the characters were well explored. What I didn't like was that most of the characters, with the exception of Ramses (The Mummy) and Elliott, Lord Rutherford, were very flat and one-dimensional. Also, the lack of detail about the surroundings the characters were in really bothered me; I had a hard time filling in the blanks and was frequently guessing. I think this was so noticeable to me because I have recently read other novels (in particular, Gone With The Wind) in which I could very literally see what was happening because of the high quality, interesting descriptions. I found this novel very lacking in this regard. Finally, I found that although the beginning of the story held my attention, the rest was really rather slow and was more of a romance novel than horror or historical. I had the distinct impression that this was more of a "sweep me off my feet" fantasy for the author than anything else, and I agree with other reviewers that state that the story seemed more like an outline and that the ending was unfinished. I didn't hate it but I didn't love it either. If you like Anne Rice and fantasy, go ahead and read it. I was just glad I found it at Goodwill.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17934704960175804345">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9454388808682706181">La 'mummia' di un romanzo, forse.<br />Da premettere che la prima parte mi era piaciuta: l'idea di partenza è affascinante. Già dopo primi capitoli però, l'autrice inizia a perdersi in assurde ripetizioni, diventa incoerente, scostante, tutta la storia acquista un'inverosimiglianza quasi inaccettabile. Ogni singolo sviluppo si basa sul presupposto che tutti i personaggi, chi più chi meno (ma io sarei propensa per il più), siano affetti da una acuta forma di demenza. <br />Julie è come se non esistesse, una</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9454388808682706181">La 'mummia' di un romanzo, forse.<br />Da premettere che la prima parte mi era piaciuta: l'idea di partenza è affascinante. Già dopo primi capitoli però, l'autrice inizia a perdersi in assurde ripetizioni, diventa incoerente, scostante, tutta la storia acquista un'inverosimiglianza quasi inaccettabile. Ogni singolo sviluppo si basa sul presupposto che tutti i personaggi, chi più chi meno (ma io sarei propensa per il più), siano affetti da una acuta forma di demenza. <br />Julie è come se non esistesse, una completa rammollita, tanto il faraone del cavolo fa lo stesso quello che vuole; i rimorsi, i sensi di colpa, tutte cose da tenere in considerazione per due, tre pagine fino a raggiungere intollerabili gradi di commiserazione vengono poi gettati al vento come nulla fosse. Puff; Alex è talmente stupido, ma talmente stupido, che quando si accorge che la donna del mistero si comporta esattamente come Ramses, non solo collega i due, ma dimentica subito questo improvviso exploit della sua intelligenza, e non si insospettisce minimamente! Bah. <br />E pensare che me lo avevano consigliato caldamente. E pensare che se quei duemila anni nella tomba non avessero causato a Ramses gravi danni cerebrali sarebbe anche stato un personaggio interessante (sotto molti punti di vista!). <br />Un'idea di fondo sviluppata molto male, in pratica.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1481008733542048155">Rating: 3.5/5 stars<br /><br />I really loved the beginning of this book, it was interesting, mysterious, and I liked the tempo. However, as the book moved into Part 2, my enjoyment lessened. I still wanted to find out what was going to happen, but I wasn't enjoying the journey to get there very much, and I thought the ending was a bit lackluster. I'm still glad I read it, I just wish the ending had lived up to what the beginning promised. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14134895266452865960">I loved this book so much! I have read it several times, and I read it again when I traveled to Egypt because part of the book takes place where I would be visiting. Most Anne Rice fans were not thrilled by it because it was so out of character for her. One friend, a Rice enthusiast, said this was her worst book because it was no more than a trashy romance. But that's why I loved it! It is a historical romance that is incredibly well-written. Basically, Rice started writing paranormal romance be</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14134895266452865960">I loved this book so much! Most Anne Rice fans were not thrilled by it because it was so out of character for her. One friend, a Rice enthusiast, said this was her worst book because it was no more than a trashy romance. But that's why I loved it! It is a historical romance that is incredibly well-written. Basically, Rice started writing paranormal romance before it was in style. Highly recommended to any fans of paranormal romance. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13648919187278619604">I'd forgotten all about having read this until I was poking around to see Anne Rice's latest offerings. I really liked this book because it was very creepy, and did not make the idea of immortal mummies "pretty", it definitely strayed into Stephen King horror area in some of its descriptions. The other thing I liked about it was that it became very philosophical about what immortality might mean and whether it was something to be idealized or avoided at all costs. No cut and dried (ha ha) answer</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13648919187278619604">I'd forgotten all about having read this until I was poking around to see Anne Rice's latest offerings. I really liked this book because it was very creepy, and did not make the idea of immortal mummies "pretty", it definitely strayed into Stephen King horror area in some of its descriptions. The other thing I liked about it was that it became very philosophical about what immortality might mean and whether it was something to be idealized or avoided at all costs. No cut and dried (ha ha) answer is offered here, you are allowed to reach your own conclusions.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3214708593643821671">At 4.5/5 stars, the Mummy stands out as one of Ms. Rice's best standalone novels, and is even better than some of her Vampire books (the later ones, anyway) The read is entertaining and the characters are fluid. Not everyone might like this book, but the descriptions have the flair Ms. Rice used to have before her novels started to go sour (around Blackwood Farm/Blood Canticle) and I definitely loved reading this book. I would give this book a perfect 5 stars if Ms. Rice had gone through with he</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3214708593643821671">At 4.5/5 stars, the Mummy stands out as one of Ms. Rice's best standalone novels, and is even better than some of her Vampire books (the later ones, anyway) The read is entertaining and the characters are fluid. Not everyone might like this book, but the descriptions have the flair Ms. Rice used to have before her novels started to go sour (around Blackwood Farm/Blood Canticle) and I definitely loved reading this book. I would give this book a perfect 5 stars if Ms. Rice had gone through with her message at the end of this book and made a sequel.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5973245250737884711">I think it says something about a book when even the subject matter fails to make me like it. I like all things ancient history related (especially Egypt) and so l jumped at the chance to read this when I spotted it in my high school library. Sadly, as this particular title was my first foray into the works of Anne Rice, I've been put off the idea of reading her books for a very long time.<br /><br />Ramses builds on the idea that the Pharaoh Ramses (historically known as one of the greatest Pharaohs to hav</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5973245250737884711">I think it says something about a book when even the subject matter fails to make me like it. I like all things ancient history related (especially Egypt) and so l jumped at the chance to read this when I spotted it in my high school library. Sadly, as this particular title was my first foray into the works of Anne Rice, I've been put off the idea of reading her books for a very long time.<br /><br />Ramses builds on the idea that the Pharaoh Ramses (historically known as one of the greatest Pharaohs to have ever lived) has consumed some magical substance that makes him immortal and so was able to lead the Kingdom of Egypt through its most industrious period. <br /><br />As he willingly wanted to take a break from living, he had ordered his priests to lock him away in a pyramid with his existence being passed on as award of mouth through the Pharaohs of Egypt in that he can be awoken to help them when Egypt-is in peril. He is later awoken by Cleopatra but then goes back to his pyramid after she dies.<br /><br />The gist of the plot is that Ramies is awoken by a team of Victorian archaeologists by accident when they ransack his pyramid and take his sarcophagus back to England with them and his developing a romantic relationship with the lead archaeologist's daughter. With all the backstory of how he came to being found by them being told in flashback.<br /><br />This book made me feel like was reading a book version of “The Mummy" only in this case being told mainly from the mummy's point-of -view and with the mummy as being a good guy and teaching the Victorians the hypocritical nature of Victorian values. As I’m not a particularly big fan of ‘bodice rippers’ I can’t say if I was particularly impressed by the romance in it.<br /><br />The language is pretty simple but at least the premise and descriptions are OK enough to maintain some interest despite the obviousness of the plot and the movie stereotypical-ness of the characters.<br /><br />So obviously nowhere near as good as Interview with the Vampire (according to my friends who have read the book-but I haven't gotten around to it yet).<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5973245250737884711">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/3501967?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 30, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/219286-lynn" class="user" title="Lynn">Lynn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/43782.The_Mummy" title=" 9780099471370" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone who loves Egypt and Ms. Rice</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/219286-lynn?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer3501967">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14813785274043360775">This is my absolute all time favorite book by Anne Rice! She introduced me to a new kind of mummy that was actually attractive. It's not your typical "Mummy" style story. The intro of Cleopatra really threw me for a loop. Anne Rice's "The Mummy" inspired me to write my own novel. You can feel the characters and see the surroundings so vividly. Her twist on the "Mummy" was a surprising and pleasant shock! <br />I must have read this novel 10 times in the last few years. Recommend it to everyone!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

Now, Katherine Ramsland, Anne Rice\'s biographer, has completely revised and updated the ultimate reference guide to the world, history, and adventures of these haunting characters, from the unforgettable Lestat to Rice\'s newest chilling creation, Memnoch the Devil.Written with the full cooperation of Anne Rice -- and now with more than 1,200 entries -- The Vampire Companion offers an insightful exploration, appreciation, and interpretation of all the characters and events, names and places, symbols and themes in the five volumes of The Vampire Chronicles, including more than one hundred pages of new entries on Rice\'s latest vampire novel, Memnoch the Devil. As a descendent of the Countess Elizabeth Bathory, he is heir to all that is wonderful and terrible about his country and his family\'s past. Codrescu brilliantly explores Drake\'s anguish, as he realizes the truth behind his gruesome family history. But more importantly, Codrescu also creates a convincing and historically accurate picture of a sadistic woman obsessed with youth, vigor, beauty, and blood_a woman with enough power to order the But his life changed when he failed to notice an explosive device that ended up maiming the captain of his Force Recon Company, a respected Marine who nearly sacrificed himself to save John\'s life.\n\nHome from Iraq, John pays a visit to his former captain, only to discover the captain has been gruesomely murdered. John pursues a strange man he sees running from the scene, but he discovers that Alex Martin is not the murderer. Alex is, in fact, the former captain\'s secret male lover and the killer\'s intended next victim.\n\nWhen it becomes clear that local law enforcement has direct connections to the murder itself, John realizes that to repay his debt of honor, he must teach Alex Martin how to protect himself, even if that means teaching Alex to kill. In the process, John confronts the painful truth about the younger brother he was unable to protect and the older sister he always felt he failed.\n\n&amp;quot;Blind Fall&amp;quot; is a story of honor and integrity, of turning failure into victory. Gordon Melton has the credentials: he\'s a religious historian, author of 25 books about religion and vampires, president of the American chapter of the Transylvania Society of Dracula (founded in Bucharest, Romania), and chairman of the committee that put on Dracula \'97: A Centennial Celebration in Los Angeles. \n\nThe Vampire Book is meticulously researched and well organized. Included are an article on the cultural history of the vampire; a historical timeline; addresses of vampire societies all over the world; a 55-page filmography; vampires in plays, opera, and ballet; a 13-page list of vampire novels; and an extensive index. \n\nThe A to Z entries, each with a short bibliography, include vampire lore in more than 30 different geographic regions and a comprehensive &amp;quot;who\'s who,&amp;quot; and cover topics ranging from fingernails to sexuality, the Camarilla to Szekelys.&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a data-text-id=\"4713113630270065913\" href=\"#\"     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice">About Anne Rice</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice"><img alt="7577" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1383250078p2/7577.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer12782582098420665950">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&amp;query=The+Vampire+Chronicles">The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a title="Stan Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice">Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold near</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12782582098420665950">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&amp;query=The+Vampire+Chronicles">The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a title="Stan Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice">Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold nearly 100 million copies, making her one of the most widely read authors in modern history.<br /><br />She uses the pseudonym <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17553.Anne_Rampling">Anne Rampling</a> for adult-themed fiction (i.e., erotica) and <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/author/show/437669.A_N_Roquelaure">A.N. Roquelaure</a> for fiction featuring sexually explicit sado-masochism.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12782582098420665950">...more</a>

    </div>
